<span id="freeTextContainer1618993027685882184">It's funny, while rereading these I'm noticing that Anita is kind of a hypocrite. Maybe because I'm older now then when I last read them but I'm seeing Anita in a whole new light. But luckily, because there's so many other characters that I still love, it didn't hinder my enjoyment of the series.<br/><br/>In this installment, Anita is dealing with the fallout of having left for almost 6 months while trying to get her metaphysical shit together. And of course, when she comes back she expects everyone to ju</span>
  <span id="freeText1618993027685882184" style="display:none">It's funny, while rereading these I'm noticing that Anita is kind of a hypocrite. Maybe because I'm older now then when I last read them but I'm seeing Anita in a whole new light. But luckily, because there's so many other characters that I still love, it didn't hinder my enjoyment of the series.<br /><br />In this installment, Anita is dealing with the fallout of having left for almost 6 months while trying to get her metaphysical shit together. And of course, when she comes back she expects everyone to just be happy that she's back and she doesn't understand that she left people in some pretty effed up situations. I think this is what annoyed me the most. Just how she didn't understand why people were mad at her for just ditching them? I was so happy when Jean-Claude called her out of her naivete. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30248.Narcissus_in_Chains__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___10_" title="Narcissus in Chains (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #10) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Narcissus in Chains</a> also introduces a new character - well, many new characters - but one important one - Micah. I remember when I first read this book, I hated Micah with a fiery passion. But now, I've come to like his character - even though I still think he's extremely passive. <br /><br />I can easily understand people's qualms when it comes to this series but I still love it and I will continue my reread because I really want to get caught back up.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1398916505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2087707746168314318">3 / 5<br/><br/>Ah, the <i>ardeur</i> rears its over-sexed head. I'm not the biggest fan of this turn in the series, but it's not a deal breaker for me. I'm a mildly sex-repulsed asexual, so I normally end up skimming the sexy bits anyways, so it doesn't really effect me.<br/><br/>I love that we get to see the repercussions of Anita's absence in St. Louis from the previous book. Jean-Claude's power base has weakened considerably, and the direction Richard is trying to take the pack in is shaky to say the least. Anita had a</span>
  <span id="freeText2087707746168314318" style="display:none">3 / 5<br /><br />Ah, the <i>ardeur</i> rears its over-sexed head. I'm not the biggest fan of this turn in the series, but it's not a deal breaker for me. I'm a mildly sex-repulsed asexual, so I normally end up skimming the sexy bits anyways, so it doesn't really effect me.<br /><br />I love that we get to see the repercussions of Anita's absence in St. Louis from the previous book. Jean-Claude's power base has weakened considerably, and the direction Richard is trying to take the pack in is shaky to say the least. Anita had a lot of personal growth in the last book, but now has to grow as 1/3 of her metaphysical triumvirate.<br /><br />The introduction of Micah is always a weird one for me. I, much like Anita, have some reservations about her... overly warm welcome, even though it's all explained. He's a great addition to the series however, and a breath of fresh air compared to all the other alpha type guy.<br /><br />The mystery in this one kinda bored me though, hence the rating. It felt a little like the mystery in Circus of the Damned, where they dangle something mildly interesting, but ultimately the baddie reveal is kind of a letdown. Chimera was an interesting concept as a villain, but felt a little unfinished. Like, he just shows up at the end and you don't have enough time with him to really appreciate any complexity. While this book could've done with some more editing when it comes to the multiple plotlines, it's still an entertaining read.</span>

<div id="review_35014369" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35014369" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1605591-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252166169p2/1605591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35014369?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/1605591-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer35014369&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer35014369" class="readable"

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17822667421946304869">I liked most of the previous Anita Blake books (the exception being <i>Blue Moon</i>), but this really is were the series shifts. The hint at the end of <i>OB</i> that Anita wants to get her life under control is not fulfilled here. In fact, it is almost like Anita has become a totally different character. There is no real plot to this book, honestly. The melding that occurs seems to have been pointless, and just made Anita weaker, in the form of enslaving her to sex. Considering that Hamilton always teased w</span>
  <span id="freeText17822667421946304869" style="display:none">I liked most of the previous Anita Blake books (the exception being <i>Blue Moon</i>), but this really is were the series shifts. The hint at the end of <i>OB</i> that Anita wants to get her life under control is not fulfilled here. In fact, it is almost like Anita has become a totally different character. There is no real plot to this book, honestly. The melding that occurs seems to have been pointless, and just made Anita weaker, in the form of enslaving her to sex. Considering that Hamilton always teased with the idea of Anita being in a real relationship with two men at once, there seems no point to having Anita gain the ardeur, unless it is to have her sleep with more than two men. This makes it a bad plot device. But my main problem is that in the hardcover edition, the Anita/Micah shower sexual encounter shows it as a rape, and then I am suppose to believe Anita loves Micah? Anita from the earlier books would have, at the very least, shot Michah or turned him into the cops at the end of the books. If you are looking for a book that is just pointless sex, read this. If you are look for a book that deals with a plot that has sex, and handles sex and rape in an adult manner, this is not the book for you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17822667421946304869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_119783297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119783297" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119783297?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119783297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10862562236279488720">Tenth in the Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter horror/urban fantasy series and revolving around Anita, a necromancer and totally conflicted woman.<br/><br/>It's been a six weeks since <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/190361.Obsidian_Butterfly' target='_blank' title='Opens Laurell K. Hamilton's Obsidian Butterly in Goodreads' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>Obsidian Butterfly</em>
</a>, 9.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>Hamilton does crack me up with her sense of humor. I love Anita's snark whether its actually said or she simply thinks it.<br/><blockquote>"...other girl talk … pretty ordinary talk. Sex, guys, turning thirty, vampires, werewolves. You know, the usual."</blockquote>While Anita does tick me off with her self-righteous, holier-th</span>
  <span id="freeText10862562236279488720" style="display:none">Tenth in the Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter horror/urban fantasy series and revolving around Anita, a necromancer and totally conflicted woman.<br /><br />It's been a six weeks since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/190361.Obsidian_Butterfly" target="_blank" title="Opens Laurell K. Hamilton's Obsidian Butterly in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Obsidian Butterfly</em>
</a>, 9.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />Hamilton does crack me up with her sense of humor. I love Anita's snark whether its actually said or she simply thinks it.<br /><blockquote>"...other girl talk … pretty ordinary talk. Sex, guys, turning thirty, vampires, werewolves. You know, the usual."</blockquote>While Anita does tick me off with her self-righteous, holier-than-thou approach to the men in her life, I appreciate that she's capable of change. Able to absorb new information and change her mind to accept truths. Ronnie, now, she's really buggin' me with her sanctimonious pronouncements. A friend is supposed to be supportive. To say <em>no</em>, to push you to reconsider bad choices. Then there's being so damned stubborn and unyielding, not listening to your friend, not taking her lessons or experiences into account.<br /><br />Anita's hypocrisy drives me nuts:<br /><blockquote>Tell me the truth, but not if it pisses me off. <br />Why didn't you tell me this would happen, but yes, I'd have wanted to kill you if you had. <br />Richard should have counseled Louisa better, forced her to practice beforehand, but don't make Anita do it.<br />Let's worry more about appearance than about reality.<br />Yes, give me the mark so I can save you, but don't expect me to follow through on anything.<br />Don't feed on me, but don't feed on anyone else.<br />Don't sleep with anyone else, but don't sleep with me either.<br />I can sleep with anyone and everyone, you can't sleep with anyone but me.<br />And you don't get to sleep with me.</blockquote>With "I didn't know" and "I didn't understand" Anita's only rallying cries.<br /><blockquote>"You are simultaneously one of the most direct women I know, and one of the most self-deluding."</blockquote><br />What is with Anita Blake? She almost dies in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/190361.Obsidian_Butterfly" target="_blank" title="Opens Laurell K. Hamilton's Obsidian Butterly in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Obsidian Butterfly</em>
</a> due to the holes in her aura. Holes she has to fix, so she's still futzing around two weeks after she gets back from New Mexico?<br /><br />Yup, Jean-Claude has learned to be very cautious around Anita. I appreciate some of her requirements. Truth is always best. However, if it's a currency you insist upon, don't get angry when you don't like the truth. Don't blame others because you lie to yourself. Honor is always good. But whining and punishing people because you didn't ask the right questions, ignored the truth, or didn't think through possible consequences is not one of the things which I like about her. There are times I simply want to smack her upside the head. She pulls her damned blinders over her head and never considers what consequences may be to others. But then she gets angry when others do the same to her. Arghh. Then again, Jean-Claude has taught her to be suspicious.<br /><blockquote>"To give up his moral code is to give up who he is."</blockquote>Narcissus is so pushy and demanding, and Jean-Claude gets his own back on him. At last. And we learn, right along with a horrified Anita and Richard, a lot more about Jean-Claude's past. Appeasing Narcissus is Asher's opportunity to hurt Jean-Claude and explain the basis for dominance and submission.<br /><br />Jesus, it was bad enough what they did to Gregory, and their attack. There's still Nathaniel to come. And Anita finally understands the smell of weakness and defeat.<br /><br />Richard learns the negatives of the democracy he's forced onto his pack. And Anita may well kill him for it. God, Richard is so naive. Richard is just as schizo as ever wanting Anita and not wanting her. He's another like Anita in wanting his cake and eating it too. I could wish she would simply wash her hands of him. His experiment in democracy shows up for its uselessness although it does provide a lovely platform for the ideal of shifter harmony. <br /><br />What's worse is Anita learns of the <em>ardeur</em> and how little control she has. I have to wonder if the <em>ardeur</em> suddenly showed up because of Anita, Jean-Claude, and Richard marrying their marks and then Anita's little "accident" at Narcissus in Chains? It gets worse too as it opens Anita up to Belle Morte! Eeeeek.<br /><blockquote>"True power comes when others offer it to you and you merely accept it as a gift, not as the spoils of some personal war."</blockquote>Let me smack her! Please, let me whap her upside the head a few times...please, please, please…! She makes me so nuts. Why must she always fight so damn hard? She hears what Jean-Claude tells her, and I swear, she doesn't take it in. Doesn't apply it to herself.<br /><br />I love the show Anita and her pard put on at the lupanar! Just goes to show what can be done! A nice poke in the eye for Jacob, especially when the munin come out to play.<br /><br />Ooh, talk about throwing it back in her face when Richard offers to go into the ground to rescue Gregory! Give Anita something to think about, because we all know it wouldn't cost Anita anything to kill Jacob for him.<br /><br />Ah geez, turnabout and turnabout. This time it's Richard getting all squeamish about Anita's <em>ardeur</em>.<br /><br />It is one way to remodel the kitchen.<br /><br />Hmm, we get some background on Rafael!<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />Anita has been avoiding everyone. And I mean, everyone for the past six months as she attempts to bolster her shields. Only to find that her shields are crap and everything has fallen apart in her absence.<br /><br />All of St. Louis is ripe for a takeover—the vampires, the wolves, the leopards, everyone.<br />Then the rats and swans arrive at the lupanar in support of Anita and her leopards…snicker…no one was expectin’ that one!<br /><br />Celebrating Ronnie's 30th birthday, Anita gets a call for help from Gregory to come rescue Nathaniel. And learns too late of betrayal from one of her own.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Anita Blake </strong>wears many hats: Nimir-Ra, leopard queen; lupa to the wolves; the human servant in a vampire triumvirate; munin channeler; and, necromancer.<br /><br /><strong>Ronnie Simms</strong> is her best friend, unhappily. She's also dating <strong>Dr. Louis Fane</strong>, wererat, one of Rafael's lieutenants, and Richard's best friend. <strong>Marianne</strong> is the psychic (and vargamor for the Tennessee pack) with whom Anita's been working on her meditation, learning ritual magic, and blocking the marks Jean-Claude bestowed on her and Richard.<br /><br /><strong>Jean-Claude</strong> is the vampire Master of the City and is at least 400 years old with the ability to gain power by feeding from blood or sexual energy, an incubus. As the master, he runs a number of clubs in St. Louis including the <strong>Circus of the Damned</strong> where his daytime resting place is, <strong>Guilty Pleasures</strong>, and <strong>Danse Macabre</strong>. <strong>Asher</strong>, his body horribly damaged, is his second-in-command, a former love who has chosen to remain in St. Louis while looking for the chance to hurt Jean-Claude in retaliation for how his human servant, <strong>Julianna</strong>, died. <strong>Willie McCoy</strong> was a weaselly human when Anita first knew him; now he's a weaselly vampire. <strong>Ming Die </strong>and <strong>Faust</strong> are vampires new come to St. Louis. With Anita's return to the supernatural life of St. Louis, <strong>Damian</strong> and <strong>Gretchen</strong> are both revived from their cross-locked coffins with Damian; that six-month distance has had a bad effect on him while Gretchen has been in a cross-wrapped coffin for three years now.<br /><br /><strong>Arturo</strong>, one of Belle's favorites. Belle is negotiating for <strong>Musette</strong> (a name that horrifies Asher and Jean-Claude) to come visit.<br /><br /><em>The wolves</em><br /><strong>Richard Zeeman</strong> is the third of their triumvirate, the alpha king of the <strong>Thronnos Roke Pack</strong>, and a junior high school science teacher. <strong>Jason Schulyer</strong> is Jean-Claude's little dress-up wolf (he's twenty-two now). <strong>Jamil</strong> is Sköll, Richard's chief enforcer. <strong>Shang-Da</strong> is his Hati, the other enforcer. <strong>Sylvie</strong> is his second-in-command, his Freki who sells insurance in her day job. <strong>Jacob</strong> is his new Geri, his new third. <strong>Paris</strong> is the more forward of the candidates for lupa. <strong>Irving Griswold</strong> is a reporter for the <em>St. Louis Post-Dispatch</em>, and just one of the many Anita has saved.<br /><br /><em>Wereleopards</em><br /><strong>Gregory</strong>; <strong>Zane</strong>; <strong>Vivian</strong>, she's dating <strong>Stephen</strong>, a wolf; <strong>Cherry</strong>, a former nurse; <strong>Nathaniel</strong>, a pet, even less than a slave in the BDSM world who becomes her <em>pomme de sang</em>; and, <strong>Elizabeth</strong>, who had been Gabriel's sweetie and is not playing well with others, are part of Anita's pard. <br /><br /><strong>Caleb</strong> and <strong>Micah Callahan</strong>, Nimir-Raj for the Maneater Clan who can call flesh, are the wereleopards Anita wakes up to. Micah, the leopards' Nimir-Raj to Anita's Nimir-Ra, appears and is the first "casualty" of the ardeur. A beacon to recall as we get further into the series. Seems Elizabeth invited him to be Nimir-Raj, but won't help any other way. <strong>Merle</strong> is the former leader who gave it up as Micah did a better job. Now he and <strong>Noah</strong> are Micah's bodyguards. <strong>Gina</strong> and <strong>Viola</strong> are more of Micah's.<br /><br /><em>The wererats</em><br /><strong>Dr. Lillian</strong> is a wererat who treats the shapeshifters in town. <strong>Rafael</strong> is the Rat King allied with Richard; he will bring his <strong>rodere</strong>. Some of Rafael's rats, <strong>Bobby Lee</strong> (he appears for the first time), <strong>Claudia</strong>, and <strong>Igor</strong>, serve as bodyguards for Anita. <br /><br /><em>Other shifters in St. Louis</em><br /><strong>Donovan Reece</strong> is the new swanking. <strong>Christine</strong> is a weretiger; <strong>Nilisha MacNair</strong> is Kadra of the werecobras, and she and her children, <strong>Ethan</strong> and <strong>Olivia</strong> want their husband and father, the Kashyapa, <strong>Henry MacNair</strong>, back; <strong>Boone</strong> is a werebear is missing <strong>Rebecca Morton</strong>, his Ursa; <strong>Gil</strong> is a werefox; <strong>Janet Talbot</strong> is missing her son, <strong>Andy</strong>, a weredog; and, <strong>Joseph</strong>, a werelion, is missing. His mate, <strong>Amber</strong>, is pregnant.<br /><br /><em>Regional Preternatural Investigation Team (RPIT)</em><br /><strong>Detective Sergeant Dolph Storr</strong> heads up this team with <strong>Zerbrowski</strong> as his irrepressible second. <strong>Lucille</strong> is Dolph's wife; <strong>Darrin</strong> is Dolph's oldest, a lawyer, and he's engaged to a vampire. <strong>Paul</strong> is an engineer, the youngest, and he and his wife can't have kids. <strong>Detective Clive Perry</strong> is the polite one amongst them. <strong>Detective Jessica Arnet</strong> is keeping Nathaniel busy.<br /><br /><strong>Orlando King</strong> had been one of the country's premiere bounty hunters before a shapeshifter nearly killed him.<br /><br /><em>Narcissus in Chains</em><br /><strong>Narcissus in Chains</strong> is a club run by shapeshifters and a neutral place for them. <strong>Narcissus</strong> himself is a cross-dressing hermaphrodite with a taste for pain — he can top or bottom. He's also the leader of the werehyenas, the only army allowed within the club's walls. <strong>Ulysses and Ajax</strong> are his bodyguards and they're lovers. <strong>Bacchus and Dionysus</strong> are lovers. <strong>Zeke</strong> is a werewolf.<br /><br /><em>Chimera's people</em><br /><strong>Chimera</strong> is a panwere, a lycanthrope that can take more than one form. <strong>Marco</strong> is a lion shifter. <strong>Coronus</strong> of the Black Water Clan is a snake shifter.<br /><br /><strong>Shielding</strong> goes outside one's aura. <strong>Master vampires</strong> can hide their allegiances. The <strong>munin</strong> are the pack's spirits of their dead. They are a repository of all the knowledge of the pack. <strong>Raina</strong>, the old lukoi lupa, is the munin who likes Anita best.<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />I’m not quite sure about this cover. Against a dragged-green background hang two shackles suspended from chains…they look more like stirrups at first glance. <br /><br />The title, <em>Narcissus in Chains</em>, is certainly appropriate for all the actions continue to revert back to Narcissus’ club and usually in chains. Certainly Narcissus himself ends up in chains as the Chimera takes over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10862562236279488720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_75762635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75762635" />
    <a title="Samantha (Book Lover&#39;s Cozy Cafe)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2525839-samantha-book-lover-s-cozy-cafe"><img alt="Samantha (Book Lover&#39;s Cozy Cafe)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605740985p2/2525839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75762635?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_169189980" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169189980" />
    <a title="Regina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3104032-regina"><img alt="Regina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362864551p2/3104032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169189980?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regina" href="/user/show/3104032-regina">Regina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=listened-to-audio-only">listened-to-audio-only</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=urban-fantasy-uf">urban-fantasy-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=audio-also-listened-to">audio-also-listened-to</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169189980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10023713268269109629">This is often noted as the first book in the great decline of Anita Blake, but I noticed that it many of my GR friends have given it 4/5 stars. For me, this book was a weak book. It was weak because it lacked the horror and fear element. My favorite Anita Blake books are the ones with a very strong horror background. This was also a weak book for me, because really I couldn’t figure out why there was the conflict. It seemed to be a weak set up. And finally, the back and forth between Richard and</span>
  <span id="freeText10023713268269109629" style="display:none">This is often noted as the first book in the great decline of Anita Blake, but I noticed that it many of my GR friends have given it 4/5 stars. For me, this book was a weak book. It was weak because it lacked the horror and fear element. My favorite Anita Blake books are the ones with a very strong horror background. This was also a weak book for me, because really I couldn’t figure out why there was the conflict. It seemed to be a weak set up. And finally, the back and forth between Richard and Anita was just tiresome. It added nothing to the story and honestly, if my best friend was going on and on the way Richard and Anita do – I would refuse to listen to it. Enough. Enough already. The sex didn’t bother me, but there really wasn’t a lot of it in this book. Anita’s personality was still likeable to me, even though Richard with Anita annoyed me, I still like Richard and all of the men. I do like the addition of the leopards – but when is Anita going to raise the dead again? I likely will wait a good while before I go on to #11, and I may just skip ahead to the books that have Edward and Olaf in them. <br /><br />Oh and the idea of were snakes really really disgusts me. Bleh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10023713268269109629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KcL1vKRLY5t0t+tdrGy1Tj6zhejJ+Vp1y0hzw3WYtxmLs9evfJNn0KGJC89o+/j6/E7SeYrYwyjko77dL1H5GQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WCKT9LW1pfxc07hKVh5WgXaxR171DtS5VOof0Y9RNVn6U7HnbW2ht4ntWNiSiRs1tEwQz7YvTeR7AdLP1Zh7WQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5867062941222770060">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis </span>
  <span id="freeText5867062941222770060" style="display:none">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis with her family.</span>

She<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13087931324369812302\" style=\"display:none\">Cerulean Sins, the eleventh entry in the hugely-popular Anita Blake series, finds everyone’s favorite vampire hunter keeping house and kicking butt.\n\nAnita Blake is trying to get her life back to “normal” after a break-up with her werewolf lover. She has settled into a pattern of domesticity, which means that the new man in her life, the leopard shapeshifter Micah, has no problem sharing her with Jean-Claude, Master Vampire of the City. Things are as peaceful as they ever get for someone who raises the dead, when Jean-Claude receives an unexpected and unwelcome visitor: Musette, the very beautiful, very twisted representative of the European Council of Vampires. Anita soon finds herself caught up in a dangerous game of vampire power politics.\n\nTo add to her troubles, she is asked to consult on a series of brutal killings, which seem to be the work of something un-human. The investigation leads her to Cerulean Sins, a vampire-run establishment that deals in erotic videos, videos that cater to very specific tastes. Anita knows one creature of the night who has such interests — Jean-Claude’s visitor. But if Anita brings Musette down, the repercussions could cost her everything she holds dear.\n\nOnce a sworn enemy of all monsters, Anita is now the human consort of both Master Vampire Jean Claude and leopard shapeshifter Micah. When a centuries-old vampire hits St. Louis, Anita finds herself needing all the dark forces her passion can muster to save the ones she loves.\n\nAnita Blake returns to find hell hath no fury like a
